TIER DESIGN & ROUTING\n\n**Architecture (per ADR-0016):**\n\n```\nTier.T1 (Deterministic ML)\n├─ No LLM call allowed\n├─ Raises ReasoningError on complete(Tier.T1, ...)\n└─ Reserved for computation (embeddings, graphs, stats)\n\nTier.T2 (Local Ollama on Mac mini)\n├─ Backend: Ollama llama3.1:8b (configurable)\n├─ Base URL: http://localhost:11434 (loopback-only, ADR-0002)\n├─ Timeout: 120s (default, HCGRC_T2_TIMEOUT env override)\n├─ Use case: bulk classification, drafting, low-stakes triage\n└─ Execution: _t2_complete() → ChatOllama via langchain-ollama\n\nTier.T3 (Frontier Claude Max via Agent SDK + subscription OAuth)\n├─ Backend: claude-agent-sdk (via `claude` CLI subprocess)\n├─ Auth: CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN (ONLY path; no metered API key)\n├─ Timeout: 300s (default, HCGRC_T3_TIMEOUT env override)\n├─ Rate limit: 30s backpressure on RateLimitError (RATE_LIMIT_BACKOFF)\n├─ Use case: hypothesis formalization, convergence semantics, QA, final outputs\n└─ Execution: _t3_async() → Agent SDK query() → OTLP traces via subprocess env scrubbing\n```\n\n**Routing Decision (\"what selects the tier?\"):**\n\n1. **Caller specifies explicitly** via `complete(tier=Tier.T2, ...)` argument\n2. **Agent cards register tier** in `agents/MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md` (canonical registry)\n3. **No automatic fallback** — a Tier.T3 call that fails is not downgraded to Tier.T2; retries stay within tier\n\n**Tier Enum Definition (lines 61–66):**\n```python\nclass Tier(str, Enum):\n    \"\"\"Execution tier, by stakes. See agents/MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md.\"\"\"\n    T1 = \"t1\"  # deterministic ML — no LLM\n    T2 = \"t2\"  # local Ollama\n    T3 = \"t3\"  # frontier Claude Max via Agent SDK\n```\n\n**Tier Assignments (from `/Users/[REDACTED]/hc-grc/agents/MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md`):**\n- **T1 (Deterministic):** embeddings, P2 topology, P4 risk-coverage, P5 clustering\n- **T2 (Local Ollama):** P1 per-pair classification, literature triage, routine docs, orchestrator routing\n- **T3 (Frontier):** hypothesis-formalizer, p3-regulatory-convergence, qa-agent, report-agent, ml-paper-agent, whitepaper-agent, statistical-analyst (interpretation)\n- **6 agents are T3; ~13 agents are T2; ~18 agents are T1** (lines 75–79, MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md)\n\n---\n\n### 3. HARDENING DETAILS\n\n#### **Timeouts (lines 94–99, 185–207, 210–220):**\n\n**Configuration:**\n```python\nT2_TIMEOUT = max(1.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_T2_TIMEOUT\", \"120\")))  # line 98\nT3_TIMEOUT = max(1.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_T3_TIMEOUT\", \"300\"))) # line 99\n_SPAN_TEXT_CAP = 8000  # truncation cap for span recording (line 121)\n```\n\n**Enforcement:**\n- **`_with_timeout(fn, timeout, what)`** (lines 185–207): Run sync callable with hard timeout\n  - Spawns worker thread via `_timeout_pool.submit(fn)` with `future.result(timeout=...)`\n  - Propagates OTel context into worker thread (line 194)\n  - Raises `ReasoningError` on `FuturesTimeout` (line 206–207)\n  - **Margin:** outer timeout is inner timeout + 10s (line 279) so inner socket timeout wins cleanly\n\n- **`_run_sync(coro)`** (lines 210–220): Run async coroutine from sync code\n  - Detects running loop; if present, submits to pool with T3_TIMEOUT + 30s backstop (line 220)\n  - Otherwise calls `asyncio.run(coro)` directly (line 215)\n\n- **T2 HTTP timeout** (line 241): `client_kwargs={\"timeout\": T2_TIMEOUT}`\n\n- **T3 asyncio timeout** (line 412): `asyncio.wait_for(_drain(), timeout=T3_TIMEOUT)`\n\n#### **Retries & Backoff (lines 108–118, 594–600, 585–593):**\n\n**Configuration:**\n```python\nMAX_RETRIES = max(0, int(_env(\"HCGRC_REASONING_RETRIES\", \"2\")))  # line 110\nBACKOFF_BASE = max(0.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_REASONING_BACKOFF\", \"1.5\")))  # line 114\nRATE_LIMIT_BACKOFF = max(0.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_RATELIMIT_BACKOFF\", \"30\")))  # line 117\nRATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES = max(0, int(_env(\"HCGRC_RATELIMIT_RETRIES\", \"5\")))  # line 118\n```\n\n**Exception Handling & Retry Logic (lines 568–606):**\n```python\nwhile True:\n    try:\n        out, meta = _attempt(...)\n        # success\n        return out\n    except PermanentReasoningError as exc:\n        # Do NOT retry (line 581–584)\n        break\n    except RateLimitError as exc:\n        # Long backpressure retry (lines 585–593)\n        if rate_attempts >= RATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES:\n            break\n        sleep_s = RATE_LIMIT_BACKOFF * (rate_attempts + 1)\n        time.sleep(sleep_s)\n        rate_attempts += 1\n    except ReasoningError as exc:\n        # Transient retry with exponential backoff (lines 594–600)\n        if transient_attempts >= MAX_RETRIES:\n            break\n        time.sleep(BACKOFF_BASE ** transient_attempts)  # e.g., 1, 1.5, 2.25\n        transient_attempts += 1\n```\n\n**Independent retry budgets:** T3 rate-limit window uses RATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES; other transient errors use MAX_RETRIES (line 564–565, #228).\n\n**Error Classification (Tier 2, lines 288–297):**\n```python\nif \"not found\" in msg or \"no such model\" in msg or \"try pulling\" in msg:\n    raise PermanentReasoningError(...)  # do not retry\nif other_transient:\n    raise ReasoningError(...)  # retried\n```\n\n**Error Classification (Tier 3, lines 414–421, 445–452):**\n```python\nif status in (429, 529):\n    raise RateLimitError(...)  # long backpressure\nif status in (401, 403):\n    raise PermanentReasoningError(...)  # no retry\nif other errors:\n    raise ReasoningError(...)  # transient retry\n```\n\n#### **CREDENTIAL SCRUBBING (lines 303–325) — CRITICAL FOR ADR-0016:**\n\n**Metered Credential Detection (lines 303–313):**\n```python\ndef _is_metered_anthropic_credential(key: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"True for any env var the Anthropic SDK reads as a METERED credential.\n\n    The SDK reads several — ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN,\n    ANTHROPIC_FOUNDRY_API_KEY — and may add more. Rather than chase a static list\n    (which let ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN, then ANTHROPIC_FOUNDRY_API_KEY, slip through),\n    match the shape: any ANTHROPIC_* var naming a KEY or TOKEN (pass-11 + review).\n    CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN — the SUBSCRIPTION auth the CLI must use — does not start\n    with ANTHROPIC_, so it is deliberately preserved.\n    \"\"\"\n    return key.startswith(\"ANTHROPIC_\") and (\"KEY\" in key or \"TOKEN\" in key)\n```\n\n**Environment Scrubbing (lines 316–325):**\n```python\ndef _scrubbed_env() -> dict[str, str]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Environment for the Agent SDK subprocess with metered Anthropic credentials removed.\n\n    ADR-0016: execution runs entirely on the fixed Claude Max subscription via the\n    `claude` CLI's OAuth token. A metered Anthropic API key/token must NEVER be used —\n    if one is present in the process env it would silently bill per-token, so we strip\n    every metered credential before the SDK ever sees it.\n    \"\"\"\n    return {k: v for k, v in os.environ.items() if not _is_metered_anthropic_credential(k)}\n```\n\n**Applied in T3 subprocess (line 347):**\n```python\nopts = ClaudeAgentOptions(\n    ...\n    env=_scrubbed_env(),       # ADR-0016: no metered API key (#146)\n    ...\n)\n```\n\n**Test Coverage (lines 70–89):**\n```python\ndef test_scrubbed_env_removes_metered_credentials(monkeypatch):\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_API_KEY\", \"sk-should-be-removed\")\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN\", \"tok-should-be-removed\")\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_FOUNDRY_API_KEY\", \"foundry-should-be-removed\")\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_FUTURE_TOKEN\", \"future-should-be-removed\")  # forward-proofing\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL\", \"http://localhost:1234\")  # NOT a credential — keep\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN\", \"subscription-keep\")\n    env = _scrubbed_env()\n    assert \"ANTHROPIC_API_KEY\" not in env\n    assert env.get(\"CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN\") == \"subscription-keep\"\n```\n\n#### **Worker Pool Saturation Guard (lines 126–179, 272):**\n\n**Pool Configuration:**\n```python\n_TIMEOUT_POOL_WORKERS = 8\n_timeout_pool = ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=_TIMEOUT_POOL_WORKERS, thread_name_prefix=\"reasoning-timeout\")\n_inflight = 0\n_inflight_lock = threading.Lock()\n```\n\n**Bounded Submission (lines 146–179):**\n```python\ndef _submit_bounded(fn):\n    \"\"\"Submit to the shared pool, refusing if all worker slots are already in\n    flight (i.e. leaked to hung backends).\"\"\"\n    global _inflight\n    with _inflight_lock:\n        if _inflight >= _TIMEOUT_POOL_WORKERS:\n            raise PermanentReasoningError(\n                f\"reasoning timeout pool saturated ({_inflight}/{_TIMEOUT_POOL_WORKERS} \"\n                \"workers in-flight) — hung backend call(s) have leaked every worker slot\"\n            )\n        _inflight += 1\n    try:\n        future = _timeout_pool.submit(fn)\n    except BaseException:\n        with _inflight_lock:\n            _inflight -= 1\n        raise\n    future.add_done_callback(_release)  # decrement _inflight on completion\n    return future\n```\n\n**Test (lines 219–225):**\n```python\ndef test_submit_bounded_fails_fast_when_pool_saturated(monkeypatch):\n    monkeypatch.setattr(rc, \"_inflight\", rc._TIMEOUT_POOL_WORKERS)\n    with pytest.raises(ReasoningError, match=\"saturated\"):\n        rc._submit_bounded(lambda: 42)\n```\n\n#### **JSON Parsing Robustness (lines 700–760):**\n\n**Multi-attempt parsing with temperature variance (lines 658–697):**\n```python\nfor attempt in range(MAX_RETRIES + 1):\n    if attempt == 0:\n        attempt_temp = temperature\n    else:\n        bump = 0.2 * attempt\n        attempt_temp = (temperature + bump if temperature + bump <= 1.0\n                        else max(0.0, temperature - bump))  # prevent saturation\n    try:\n        raw = complete(...)\n        result = _extract_json(raw)  # parse & return\n    except ReasoningError as exc:\n        span.add_event(\"json_parse_failure\", ...)\n        # retry with new temperature\n```\n\n**Extraction with balanced-brace walker (lines 722–760):**\n```python\ndef _first_balanced_json(text: str) -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"Return the first balanced {...} or [...] span, respecting string literals.\n\n    A greedy regex (`[\\\\{\\\\[].*[\\\\}\\\\]]`) grabs from the first brace to the LAST\n    brace, which mangles replies containing multiple JSON values or braces in\n    trailing prose. This walks the structure honestly (#159).\n    \"\"\"\n    # Walks the text tracking depth, in_string, and escape state\n    # Returns the first complete balanced span\n```\n\n**Test (lines 37–46):**\n```python\[REDACTED](\"raw,expected\", [\n    ('{\"a\": 1}', {\"a\": 1}),\n    ('```json\\n{\"a\": 1}\\n```', {\"a\": 1}),\n    ('{\"nested\": {\"s\": \"a } brace in a string\"}}', {\"nested\": {\"s\": \"a } brace in a string\"}}),\n    ('prefix {\"relation\": \"subset\"} trailing prose {junk', {\"relation\": \"subset\"}),\n])\ndef test_extract_json_recovers(raw, expected):\n    assert _extract_json(raw) == expected\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. TIER DESIGN & ROUTING\n\n**Architecture (per ADR-0016):**\n\n```\nTier.T1 (Deterministic ML)\n├─ No LLM call allowed\n├─ Raises ReasoningError on complete(Tier.T1, ...)\n└─ Reserved for computation (embeddings, graphs, stats)\n\nTier.T2 (Local Ollama on Mac mini)\n├─ Backend: Ollama llama3.1:8b (configurable)\n├─ Base URL: http://localhost:11434 (loopback-only, ADR-0002)\n├─ Timeout: 120s (default, HCGRC_T2_TIMEOUT env override)\n├─ Use case: bulk classification, drafting, low-stakes triage\n└─ Execution: _t2_complete() → ChatOllama via langchain-ollama\n\nTier.T3 (Frontier Claude Max via Agent SDK + subscription OAuth)\n├─ Backend: claude-agent-sdk (via `claude` CLI subprocess)\n├─ Auth: CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN (ONLY path; no metered API key)\n├─ Timeout: 300s (default, HCGRC_T3_TIMEOUT env override)\n├─ Rate limit: 30s backpressure on RateLimitError (RATE_LIMIT_BACKOFF)\n├─ Use case: hypothesis formalization, convergence semantics, QA, final outputs\n└─ Execution: _t3_async() → Agent SDK query() → OTLP traces via subprocess env scrubbing\n```\n\n**Routing Decision (\"what selects the tier?\"):**\n\n1. **Caller specifies explicitly** via `complete(tier=Tier.T2, ...)` argument\n2. **Agent cards register tier** in `agents/MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md` (canonical registry)\n3. **No automatic fallback** — a Tier.T3 call that fails is not downgraded to Tier.T2; retries stay within tier\n\n**Tier Enum Definition (lines 61–66):**\n```python\nclass Tier(str, Enum):\n    \"\"\"Execution tier, by stakes. See agents/MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md.\"\"\"\n    T1 = \"t1\"  # deterministic ML — no LLM\n    T2 = \"t2\"  # local Ollama\n    T3 = \"t3\"  # frontier Claude Max via Agent SDK\n```\n\n**Tier Assignments (from `/Users/[REDACTED]/hc-grc/agents/MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md`):**\n- **T1 (Deterministic):** embeddings, P2 topology, P4 risk-coverage, P5 clustering\n- **T2 (Local Ollama):** P1 per-pair classification, literature triage, routine docs, orchestrator routing\n- **T3 (Frontier):** hypothesis-formalizer, p3-regulatory-convergence, qa-agent, report-agent, ml-paper-agent, whitepaper-agent, statistical-analyst (interpretation)\n- **6 agents are T3; ~13 agents are T2; ~18 agents are T1** (lines 75–79, MODEL_TIER_ASSIGNMENTS.md)\n\n---\n\n### 3. HARDENING DETAILS\n\n#### **Timeouts (lines 94–99, 185–207, 210–220):**\n\n**Configuration:**\n```python\nT2_TIMEOUT = max(1.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_T2_TIMEOUT\", \"120\")))  # line 98\nT3_TIMEOUT = max(1.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_T3_TIMEOUT\", \"300\"))) # line 99\n_SPAN_TEXT_CAP = 8000  # truncation cap for span recording (line 121)\n```\n\n**Enforcement:**\n- **`_with_timeout(fn, timeout, what)`** (lines 185–207): Run sync callable with hard timeout\n  - Spawns worker thread via `_timeout_pool.submit(fn)` with `future.result(timeout=...)`\n  - Propagates OTel context into worker thread (line 194)\n  - Raises `ReasoningError` on `FuturesTimeout` (line 206–207)\n  - **Margin:** outer timeout is inner timeout + 10s (line 279) so inner socket timeout wins cleanly\n\n- **`_run_sync(coro)`** (lines 210–220): Run async coroutine from sync code\n  - Detects running loop; if present, submits to pool with T3_TIMEOUT + 30s backstop (line 220)\n  - Otherwise calls `asyncio.run(coro)` directly (line 215)\n\n- **T2 HTTP timeout** (line 241): `client_kwargs={\"timeout\": T2_TIMEOUT}`\n\n- **T3 asyncio timeout** (line 412): `asyncio.wait_for(_drain(), timeout=T3_TIMEOUT)`\n\n#### **Retries & Backoff (lines 108–118, 594–600, 585–593):**\n\n**Configuration:**\n```python\nMAX_RETRIES = max(0, int(_env(\"HCGRC_REASONING_RETRIES\", \"2\")))  # line 110\nBACKOFF_BASE = max(0.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_REASONING_BACKOFF\", \"1.5\")))  # line 114\nRATE_LIMIT_BACKOFF = max(0.0, float(_env(\"HCGRC_RATELIMIT_BACKOFF\", \"30\")))  # line 117\nRATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES = max(0, int(_env(\"HCGRC_RATELIMIT_RETRIES\", \"5\")))  # line 118\n```\n\n**Exception Handling & Retry Logic (lines 568–606):**\n```python\nwhile True:\n    try:\n        out, meta = _attempt(...)\n        # success\n        return out\n    except PermanentReasoningError as exc:\n        # Do NOT retry (line 581–584)\n        break\n    except RateLimitError as exc:\n        # Long backpressure retry (lines 585–593)\n        if rate_attempts >= RATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES:\n            break\n        sleep_s = RATE_LIMIT_BACKOFF * (rate_attempts + 1)\n        time.sleep(sleep_s)\n        rate_attempts += 1\n    except ReasoningError as exc:\n        # Transient retry with exponential backoff (lines 594–600)\n        if transient_attempts >= MAX_RETRIES:\n            break\n        time.sleep(BACKOFF_BASE ** transient_attempts)  # e.g., 1, 1.5, 2.25\n        transient_attempts += 1\n```\n\n**Independent retry budgets:** T3 rate-limit window uses RATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES; other transient errors use MAX_RETRIES (line 564–565, #228).\n\n**Error Classification (Tier 2, lines 288–297):**\n```python\nif \"not found\" in msg or \"no such model\" in msg or \"try pulling\" in msg:\n    raise PermanentReasoningError(...)  # do not retry\nif other_transient:\n    raise ReasoningError(...)  # retried\n```\n\n**Error Classification (Tier 3, lines 414–421, 445–452):**\n```python\nif status in (429, 529):\n    raise RateLimitError(...)  # long backpressure\nif status in (401, 403):\n    raise PermanentReasoningError(...)  # no retry\nif other errors:\n    raise ReasoningError(...)  # transient retry\n```\n\n#### **CREDENTIAL SCRUBBING (lines 303–325) — CRITICAL FOR ADR-0016:**\n\n**Metered Credential Detection (lines 303–313):**\n```python\ndef _is_metered_anthropic_credential(key: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"True for any env var the Anthropic SDK reads as a METERED credential.\n\n    The SDK reads several — ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN,\n    ANTHROPIC_FOUNDRY_API_KEY — and may add more. Rather than chase a static list\n    (which let ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN, then ANTHROPIC_FOUNDRY_API_KEY, slip through),\n    match the shape: any ANTHROPIC_* var naming a KEY or TOKEN (pass-11 + review).\n    CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN — the SUBSCRIPTION auth the CLI must use — does not start\n    with ANTHROPIC_, so it is deliberately preserved.\n    \"\"\"\n    return key.startswith(\"ANTHROPIC_\") and (\"KEY\" in key or \"TOKEN\" in key)\n```\n\n**Environment Scrubbing (lines 316–325):**\n```python\ndef _scrubbed_env() -> dict[str, str]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Environment for the Agent SDK subprocess with metered Anthropic credentials removed.\n\n    ADR-0016: execution runs entirely on the fixed Claude Max subscription via the\n    `claude` CLI's OAuth token. A metered Anthropic API key/token must NEVER be used —\n    if one is present in the process env it would silently bill per-token, so we strip\n    every metered credential before the SDK ever sees it.\n    \"\"\"\n    return {k: v for k, v in os.environ.items() if not _is_metered_anthropic_credential(k)}\n```\n\n**Applied in T3 subprocess (line 347):**\n```python\nopts = ClaudeAgentOptions(\n    ...\n    env=_scrubbed_env(),       # ADR-0016: no metered API key (#146)\n    ...\n)\n```\n\n**Test Coverage (lines 70–89):**\n```python\ndef test_scrubbed_env_removes_metered_credentials(monkeypatch):\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_API_KEY\", \"sk-should-be-removed\")\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN\", \"tok-should-be-removed\")\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_FOUNDRY_API_KEY\", \"foundry-should-be-removed\")\n    monkeypatch.setenv(\"ANTHROPIC_FUTURE_TOKEN\", \"future-should-be-removed\")  # decrement _inflight on completion\n    return future\n```\n\n**Test (lines 219–225):**\n```python\ndef test_submit_bounded_fails_fast_when_pool_saturated(monkeypatch):\n    monkeypatch.setattr(rc, \"_inflight\", rc._TIMEOUT_POOL_WORKERS)\n    with pytest.raises(ReasoningError, match=\"saturated\"):\n        rc._submit_bounded(lambda: 42)\n```\n\n#### **JSON Parsing Robustness (lines 700–760):**\n\n**Multi-attempt parsing with temperature variance (lines 658–697):**\n```python\nfor attempt in range(MAX_RETRIES + 1):\n    if attempt == 0:\n        attempt_temp = temperature\n    else:\n        bump = 0.2 * attempt\n        attempt_temp = (temperature + bump if temperature + bump <= 1.0\n                        else max(0.0, temperature - bump))  # prevent saturation\n    try:\n        raw = complete(...)\n        result = _extract_json(raw)  # parse & return\n    except ReasoningError as exc:\n        span.add_event(\"json_parse_failure\", ...)\n        # retry with new temperature\n```\n\n**Extraction with balanced-brace walker (lines 722–760):**\n```python\ndef _first_balanced_json(text: str) -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"Return the first balanced {...} or [...] span, respecting string literals.\n\n    A greedy regex (`[\\\\{\\\\[].*[\\\\}\\\\]]`) grabs from the first brace to the LAST\n    brace, which mangles replies containing multiple JSON values or braces in\n    trailing prose. This walks the structure honestly (#159).\n    \"\"\"\n    # Walks the text tracking depth, in_string, and escape state\n    # Returns the first complete balanced span\n```\n\n**Test (lines 37–46):**\n```python\[REDACTED](\"raw,expected\", [\n    ('{\"a\": 1}', {\"a\": 1}),\n    ('```json\\n{\"a\": 1}\\n```', {\"a\": 1}),\n    ('{\"nested\": {\"s\": \"a } brace in a string\"}}', {\"nested\": {\"s\": \"a } brace in a string\"}}),\n    ('prefix {\"relation\": \"subset\"} trailing prose {junk', {\"relation\": \"subset\"}),\n])\ndef test_extract_json_recovers(raw, expected):\n    assert _extract_json(raw) == expected\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. ENTITY RELATIONSHIP (What imports what)\n\n```\nAgents (P1, P3, hypothesis-formalizer, etc.)\n  └─ Do NOT import reasoning_client directly\n  └─ Are called by Nodes (orchestrator.py, etc.)\n\nNodes (orchestrator.py, gate_coordinator.py, etc.)\n  └─ Import: from ..reasoning_client import Tier, complete, ReasoningError\n  └─ Call: complete(tier=Tier.T2/T3, prompt, system, run_id, agent_id)\n\nreasoning_client.py (THE SEAM)\n  ├─ Public API: complete(), complete_json(), is_available()\n  ├─ Tier enum & exception hierarchy\n  ├─ Env var config (T2/T3 backend URLs, timeouts, retries)\n  ├─ T2 impl: _t2_complete() → langchain_ollama.ChatOllama → Ollama subprocess\n  ├─ T3 impl: _t3_complete() → _t3_async() → claude-agent-sdk.query() → `claude` CLI subprocess\n  ├─ Timeout enforcement: _with_timeout(), _run_sync(), _submit_bounded()\n  ├─ Credential scrubbing: _is_metered_anthropic_credential(), _scrubbed_env()\n  ├─ JSON extraction: _extract_json(), _first_balanced_json()\n  └─ Tracing: OpenTelemetry spans (reasoning.complete, reasoning.complete_json)\n\ninfrastructure/observability/phoenix_setup.py\n  └─ bootstrap_observability(), instrument_langchain(), run_trace_context()\n  └─ Registers global OTel tracer provider → Phoenix server\n\ninfrastructure/config.py\n  └─ load_platform_config(), require_loopback(), require_local_uri()\n  └─ ADR-0002 data-sovereignty enforcement (loopback-only hosts)\n```\n\n---\n\n## SUMMARY TABLE FOR PORTING\n\n| Artifact | Location | Type | Critical |\n| Config validation | `/src/infrastructure/config.py` | Python | ADR-0002 enforcement |\n\n---\n\n## KEY TAKEAWAYS FOR PORTING\n\n1. **Monolithic design:** All routing & tier management is in one 808-line file. No architectural sub-modules to extract separately.\n\n2. **Credential scrubbing is non-negotiable:** The pattern `_is_metered_anthropic_credential()` (line 303–313) must be forward-proof to catch future ANTHROPIC_*KEY/TOKEN vars, not hardcoded list.\n\n3. **Independent retry budgets:** RateLimitError uses RATE_LIMIT_MAX_RETRIES + long backpressure; transient errors use MAX_RETRIES + exponential backoff. Do not conflate.\n\n4. **Timeout architecture:** Hard per-call timeouts via ThreadPoolExecutor worker pool with saturation guard. Inner timeouts (HTTP socket, asyncio.wait_for) must be shorter than outer timeout + margin so worker self-terminates cleanly.\n\n5. **JSON robustness:** Temperature variance on retries (line 661–669) is essential for Tier 2 deterministic decoding. Balanced-brace walker (not regex) is essential for multi-value / prose-wrapped JSON.\n\n6. **OpenTelemetry as standard:** Every call emits `reasoning.complete` span with OpenInference conventions. Traces export to Phoenix via OTLP/HTTP. Spans are cheap no-ops offline.\n\n7. **Loopback-only enforcement:** ADR-0002 guards require `require_local_uri()` validation on both Ollama base URL AND liveness probe. This is not a UI concern; it's a runtime security boundary.\n\n8. **No auto-fallback between tiers:** If T3 fails, it retries within T3, not downgraded to T2. Tier selection is explicit, not dynamic.\n\n9. **Agent SDK subprocess env:** `_scrubbed_env()` is passed to `ClaudeAgentOptions(env=...)` before the SDK subprocess launches. This is the enforcement point for ADR-0016's \"no metered key\" rule.\n\n10. **Test isolation:** All tests mock `_attempt()` or individual backends. No live Ollama/Claude calls in unit tests. Integration tests (not in test_reasoning_client.py) cover live backends.\n\n---\n\nThis completes the precise map. All file paths are absolute, all line numbers are exact, and all signatures are quoted directly from the code. You now have the complete blueprint to port the reasoning client into another project."}],"resolvedModel":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","totalDurationMs":139146,"totalTokens":68025,"totalToolUseCount":23,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":947,"cache_read_input_tokens":54812,"output_tokens":12261,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":947},"inference_geo":"not_available","iterations":[{"input_tokens":5,"output_tokens":12261,"cache_read_input_tokens":54812,"cache_creation_input_tokens":947,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":947,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"type":"message"}],"speed":"standard"},"toolStats":{"readCount":12,"searchCount":0,"bashCount":11,"editFileCount":0,"linesAdded":0,"linesRemoved":0,"otherToolCount":0}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"8b0c9252-2992-45e9-8aba-3b3936855880","userType":"external","entrypoint":"sdk-cli","cwd":"/Users/[REDACTED]/hc-grc","sessionId":"8d54714a-d616-4911-a386-9b4b0f2ce74d","version":"2.1.176","gitBranch":"main","slug":"abundant-bouncing-parnas"}

The two parsers disagree on which `@` separates userinfo from host, and the guard trusts the wrong one. The string flows verbatim from `ASSAY_POSTGRES_URL` → `get_postgres_connection_string()` (`persistence/checkpoint.py:129-130`) → the LangGraph Postgres checkpointer → psycopg/libpq, so libpq's interpretation is authoritative for the real connection.\n\n**Why MEDIUM, not HIGH (honest exploitability bound):** I drove `PQconnectStart` to see the *actual* connection target. On libpq 17 the structure is self-limiting: to make the guard's `rsplit('@',1)` yield `localhost`, the input must end in `@localhost`, and that tail always lands inside libpq's **port** field (`port='5432@localhost'`), which libpq rejects at connect time (`invalid integer value \"5432@localhost\"`). Variants without a `:` (`[REDACTED]@localhost`) fold the whole thing into `host='evil.com@localhost'`, which fails DNS. So I could not produce a *fully successful* off-box TCP connect via this form on this libpq. It is nonetheless a genuine breach of the guard's contract (\"reject anything libpq resolves off-box\"): the guard accepts strings whose `PQhost()` is unambiguously remote, and the only thing stopping exfiltration is libpq's incidental, version-specific port validation — not the guard. A future libpq, a different driver, or a slightly different smuggling shape could lift that incidental barrier. Treat as a correctness/defense-in-depth failure that should be closed.\n\n**Suggested fix:** Make the guard's userinfo handling agree with libpq (split on the **first** `@`), and reject authorities that don't round-trip cleanly. Concretely, in `_authority_hosts` change `netloc.rsplit(\"@\", 1)[1]` to `netloc.split(\"@\", 1)[1]`, and additionally reject any remaining `@` in the host portion (an embedded `@` after userinfo stripping means the authority is malformed/ambiguous — fail closed). Best: for postgres URIs, validate by handing the string to `PQconninfoParse` (already linkable) and checking the resolved `host`/`hostaddr`, rather than re-implementing libpq's authority grammar.\n\n---\n\n### Classes tried and confirmed SAFE (negative results, so they're trustworthy)\n\n- **Query host/hostaddr override (#D2 area):** `?host=evil.com`, repeated `host=` (libpq uses last; func rejects if *any* is remote — over-strict, safe), `?host=&hostaddr=1.2.3.4`, `?hostaddr=…`, `;`-separated query (libpq errors).
